Finance: Foreign Exchange Market Sees a Big Upsurge Yesterday, HSBC Supply is Thin, Black Market is Chaotic, British Exchange Approaches Four Shillings, U.S. Exchange Approaches Five Yuan Mark 98

Yesterday, the foreign exchange market saw HSBC consistently shrinking its quotes. The British exchange rate was revised to 3 shillings and 2.5 pence, and the US exchange rate was posted at 4.6875 yuan. The British exchange rate has reached its tightest quoted price since August 11 of last year, and the US exchange rate even broke the record of 5.5 yuan on September 19 of last year. Other exchange rates also shrank across the board. The domestic market situation was extremely chaotic. After the opening in the morning, rumors spread everywhere, causing unnecessary anxiety. As a result, buying surged, while selling was hard to find, and no transactions were made. There was no definite market price. Around 9:30 AM, it was heard that the British exchange rate was 3 shillings and 2.5 pence, and the US exchange rate was 4.625 yuan. Because HSBC and other foreign banks did not maintain their rates, public panic increased. Later, speculators and Chinese banks took advantage of the high prices to sell long positions, and the market temporarily stabilized. Before the close of the morning session, buying decreased slightly, and there was some relaxation. However, speculators fiercely pushed prices up again in the afternoon, and the tight situation returned. The reason was that foreign banks were unwilling to sell, and the closing results were 3 shillings and 3.75 pence for British exchange and 4.875 yuan for US exchange, a sharp decrease of 75 and 1.0625 yuan compared to the previous day. The futures trend was no different from the spot market.

Market Price Only Available After 9:30 AM

In the morning, the price of large London bars rose by nearly 375, the distant ones increased by 25, the price of silver in New York remained flat, and the price of raw gold in London remained fixed. The exchange rates for British against US, Shanghai, and French currencies were all flat. The US exchange rate fell by 1.5 points against the British, 6 points against Shanghai, and 0.75 points against the French. The central government's quoted prices for various currencies remained the same. The selling prices for spot goods at bank morning closings were still 4 shillings and 125 pence and 5.9375 yuan for British and American currencies, respectively. However, the market was extremely chaotic at the time due to widespread rumors. Moreover, it was heard that HSBC and foreign banks had no intention to supply, so the public was panicked. There was buying in the market but no selling, so there were few transactions. It was not until around 9:30 AM that there was an official market price. British exchange rate was 3 shillings and 25 pence, and the US exchange rate was 4.625 yuan. The HSBC quotes were announced, with the British exchange rate changed to 3 shillings and 25 pence, and the US exchange rate to 4.6875 yuan. Other rates were reduced across the board. The silver balance tax was announced, an increase of 1.75 yuan. It was later heard that foreign banks were doing spot British exchange rate at 3 shillings and 375 pence, but the situation remained uncertain. Later, because Chinese banks and speculators profited from long positions, they came out of the market one after another, and slightly hardened. It is estimated that foreign banks absorbed spot US currency from Chinese banks at 4.8125 to 5 yuan, and soon speculators sold spot US currency to foreign banks already at 5.1875 yuan. The noon closing was still stable, with the British exchange rate being 3 shillings and a half penny, and the US exchange rate being 5.09375 yuan. The British exchange rate for the May contract was 3 shillings and 375 pence, and the US exchange rate was 4.9375 yuan, which was 625 lower for British and 84375 lower for American currencies compared to the morning opening. Futures also shrank drastically.

Still Feeling Insufficient Funds in the Afternoon

In the afternoon, speculator's purchases and tight situation revived. It is estimated that speculators had purchased the May US exchange rate from foreign banks at 4.875 yuan and 4.75 yuan. After all, foreign banks still saw thin supply, and funds were often lacking. Until the evening closing, the situation recovered slightly, with the British exchange rate at 3 shillings and 375 pence, and the US exchange rate at 4.875 yuan. There were no transactions heard for the June British exchange rate being 3 shillings and 25 pence, and the US exchange rate at 4.6875 yuan. Compared to the overnight closing, the spot British exchange rate shrank by 75, and the US shrunk by 1.0625 yuan. This month, British and American currencies each softened by 6875 and 1 yuan.

The Frenzy of Speculation: Gold Market Soars to the Heavens, Opening at a Peak Price of 6,700 Yuan 102

Yesterday, the cash "cooked red" (shà chì - slang for speculative) grey market was like a bolt from the blue, suddenly experiencing a horrifying surge. Those who heard of it were dismayed. The main reason was that speculators were spreading rumors, and operators were alarming each other, leading to an extremely tight foreign exchange market. The gold rush also surged accordingly. The market was chaotic in the early morning, opening only at 10 o'clock. Initially, bids reached 7,000 yuan, but the actual price was 6,700 yuan, a jump of 772 yuan. Later, many bullish investors took profits and exited, such as Qian Dui Ye and banks, selling heavily. In an instant, the price fell to 6,200 yuan. However, the situation suddenly improved towards the close, with the after-market opening jumping 190 yuan. This was due to the continued tightness of foreign exchange and the frantic search by gold shops and securities firms. The price even rose to 6,530 yuan, ultimately closing at 6,485 yuan, a sharp increase of 757 yuan compared to the previous day. However, according to the US dollar settlement price for the day, it was still more than 700 yuan lower. The future of gold prices is unpredictable and profound. Observing the increasing expansion of the European situation, if the United States is drawn into the war, gold may inevitably experience a reaction. Bullish investors without real strength should be cautious and prepare for the worst. The total trading volume for the day was about 5,000 taels. Jewelry gold in silver shops surged by 80 yuan, reaching an unprecedented peak price of 660 yuan. Customs gold, etc., remained flat.

"Cooked Red" Jumps 757 Yuan

From the morning, before 9 o'clock, people's minds were still stable. However, when the foreign exchange market opened at 9 o'clock, it was reported that there was a market without transactions, causing panic among the public. To avoid risks, people waited for the foreign exchange market to open before trading, so the market opened half an hour later than usual. Around 10 o'clock, a certain gold shop first bid to sell at 7,000 yuan, but at that time, only another gold shop offered to buy at 6,700 yuan. Soon, the opening price was seen at 6,700 yuan, a rare surge of 972 yuan compared to the previous day. Later, with the disappearance of buyers, the price plummeted by 200 yuan without any transactions. Afterward, with the outpouring from gold shops and silver shops, although a certain securities firm took the opportunity to absorb, the position ultimately felt full, and the price continued to fall by 250 yuan. The securities firm sold 50 taels to the bank at 6,250 yuan. Then, the bank suddenly advanced sharply, and sellers gradually decreased. The price jumped again by 250 yuan, with the bank taking 20 taels from Qian Dui Ye at 6,500 yuan. Later, as foreign exchange eased, a selling frenzy was reignited, and the securities firm suddenly reappeared. Gold shops and Qian Dui Ye also filled in, and soon the price fell back by 300 yuan. Deng Juan firm sold 30 taels to the bank at 6,200 yuan. It was heard that a few transactions were also made at 6,180 yuan, but some buyers with a limit price of 6,200 yuan did not succeed. After 11 o'clock, sellers gradually decreased, and a certain securities firm and bank suddenly started to collect, soaring the price by 190 yuan. The bank took 20 taels from the gold shop at 6,390 yuan. At that time, there were many sellers with a limit price of 6,400, and the price surge was blocked. Then, with the bank's reduced collection efforts, the price fell back by a small 130 yuan. The bank mutually transacted 30 taels at 6,260 yuan as the noon closing price. When the market opened in the afternoon, sentiment was surprisingly good. Gold shops raised prices to buy, jumping 190 yuan. The gold shop took 20 taels from the bank at 6,450 yuan. Later, the securities firm sold, immediately falling back by 70 yuan. The bank did 10 taels, at 6,380 yuan. Eventually, as foreign exchange became tight again, the securities firm suddenly advanced again, and Qian Dui Ye also bought, soaring 150 yuan. The gold shop took 30 taels from the bank at 6,512 yuan. Later, the buying frenzy gradually subsided, and gold shops suddenly intended to sell, filling in somewhat, immediately falling back by 130 yuan. The bank sold 20 taels to the securities firm at 6,400 yuan. Afterward, the securities firm came to search and purchase again, rising again. The securities firm took 20 taels from the gold shop at 6,485 yuan as the late closing price, resulting in a 757 yuan increase compared to the previous day. The price fluctuated by 500 yuan throughout the day. The selling price of cash gold from the main brand of gold shops was several tens of yuan higher than "cooked red," and the purchase price was reduced by 30 yuan. The current premium gold was more than 50 yuan lower than the listed gold, and there were few transactions.

Silver Shop Jewelry Gold Rises by 80 Yuan

The initial selling price of jewelry gold in silver shops was still 580 yuan per tael at Datong Hang. By 10 o'clock, due to the surge in "cooked red," reaching nearly 1,000 yuan, the price was also raised by 70 yuan. At 1 o'clock in the afternoon, it rose by another 10 yuan, resulting in Datong Hang changing the listed price to 660 yuan. The new peers had the same price, and the purchase price was reduced by about 30 yuan. The above prices have all created unprecedented high prices since the market's inception.

Securities: Fluctuations in Domestic Debt Not Yet Severe 103

The securities grey market yesterday suddenly experienced turbulence due to sudden changes in finance. Foreign exchange suddenly experienced extraordinary changes. In an instant, the US dollar shrank by more than one yuan, and gold soared by nearly 1,000 yuan, which was an unprecedented and strange change. It is said that the Hong Kong Foreign Exchange Equalization Fund Committee has abandoned the maintenance of the standard. All Chinese and foreign banks in Shanghai refused to supply foreign exchange, and there was talk of the establishment of a pseudo-Central Bank. The market's morale was severely impacted by this huge change, and the rapid rise in prices caused panic among most people. The tightness of silver was even worse than five days ago, and there were rumors that several silver shops were unstable. In this tense market situation, public bonds were also affected by these unfavorable news and fell. However, there were also many who wanted to buy before selling. The situation will be clear in a day or two. Yesterday, Tong Kang bought in both the morning and afternoon, especially in the afternoon. The rest were mainly covering short positions. The outflow of spot goods occurred both in the morning and afternoon. In the morning, spot goods were delivered from numbers 12, 20, 22, 35, and 38. Xinfu and Yongkang slightly covered short positions. In the afternoon, Changmao and Lianhe sold in large quantities. Hengfu and number 38 still bought out. The market price rose by several dimes in the afternoon, but ultimately fell by a small two to six dimes. About 120 yuan was transacted. A brief table is listed below:

Coal: Coal Balls Increase by 23 Yuan, 8.5 Yuan Per Dan 104

Coal ball market: Yesterday, due to the sharp contraction of shillings and drastic changes in the foreign exchange market, all factories stopped trading in the morning. An emergency meeting was held in the afternoon, resolving that, effective immediately, the factory price for the industry would increase by 23 yuan. The opening prices for Yitaixing, Nanyang, Guohua coal balls are 158 yuan per ton from the factory, 1.25 yuan per bundle, and 8.5 yuan per dan at the street door shops. The opening prices for smoke-free white coal have not yet been announced, and no transactions have been made.

Sugar Market: Foreign Exchange Contracts Sharply, Sugar Prices Soar 105

Yesterday, the sugar market experienced a sharp contraction in foreign exchange. Dutch exchange reached 8.750, then rose to 9.500 to 9.375. However, the association in this city drew the line, because the asking price of outgoing clients was too high, resulting in a lack of transactions. The spot price for Four Rivers coarse white new goods at the outer warehouse was 75 yuan, transit goods 60 yuan, Taikoo vehicle white B mark goods at the West warehouse was 85 yuan, and Dutch red 63 yuan. The degree of price increases reached about 10 yuan, so incoming clients were watching, and there were only no transactions. National sugar was also tight. It was heard that Diao Qing would open at 57-58 yuan, up 2-3 yuan, and the rest also asked for increases.

Food: Amidst the Surging Gold Rush, Rice Merchants Greatly Display Their Speculative Skills. Cargo Owners Insist on Not Releasing, Conversely Promoting Market Prices to Rise Directly. Hearing that Gold Prices Have Fallen Slightly, They Fear They Won't Be Able to Get Rid of It in Time. As a Result, Both Foreign Rice and Japonica Rice Rose by One or Two Yuan 106

Since the previous dynasty, because the expiry date has passed, the sales market of rice has become more prosperous. The prices of various kinds of foreign rice have all risen by one yuan. For example, No. 1 Saigon had already been sold for 47 yuan, and small twisted rice for 43.5 yuan. Yesterday morning, inheriting the upward momentum, people's minds were particularly firm, and buying and selling were quite prosperous. The market immediately saw high prices. When news broke that gold prices had caused an unprecedented surge of 1,000 yuan, the city was instantly filled with storms and rain. People's minds were as if selling parties insisted on not getting rid of the stocks, and they actually came out to turn in the gains they made. The market was agitated for a time, and the shouting was chaotic. The market prices of various kinds of foreign rice increased sharply, with No. 1 Saigon reaching a maximum peak of 49 yuan, No. 2 at 47.5 yuan, and small twisted rice at 46.5 yuan, a sharp increase of three yuan compared to the previous market. From morning to noon, there was no slight setback, and it was not until the close of the market that news suddenly broke that gold prices had fallen back by 400 yuan that the market began to flag. Because the changes were so drastic, the resistance was also strong. If people's minds were not discouraged, then everything was fine, but if they were discouraged, the overall situation would be affected. At that time, everyone insisted on recovering losses, using every means to the extreme. By this time, they were afraid that they would not be able to get rid of the stocks in time, and they returned them one after another, causing a reverse situation to the early market, showing only release and no input, and market prices dropped step by step, suddenly shedding about 1.5 yuan. In the end, the market closed weakly, with a total increase of two yuan compared to the previous increase. No. 1 Saigon was 48 yuan, and small twisted rice was 40-45.5 yuan.

Although there were more than 2,000 packages of thick and thin japonica and other domestic rice arriving, because foreign rice soared, they were able to keep pace. Trading in the market was also changed to an off-market grey market. Because the price was lower than that of foreign rice, transactions were particularly numerous. Although they were also raised with each other, they were ultimately not as large as that of foreign rice, only rising or falling by one or two yuan. Transactions for Xibang special Qing japonica were 48 yuan, general market 47 yuan, powder japonica 46 yuan, Chang Kun white japonica 47.5 to 45.5 yuan, Qing Si special thin 47 yuan wholesale, general market 45-6 yuan, Zhongguan around 44 yuan, Nanhai early rice 45 yuan, special 46 yuan, secondary 43 yuan, Hu Jian 41-2 yuan.

Although the sales market for glutinous rice was not as wide as that of other goods, its price was the cheapest, and there were also large households hoarding and collecting, so market prices were also good. The price of Liyang special yuan was 41.5 yuan, general market 40 yuan, Chang Dan goods from 40 yuan, secondary to around 38 yuan.

Foreign rice was suppressed by the tightness of fourth-bottom funds, making it difficult to rise. In recent weeks, it has been difficult to revitalize. After the fourth-bottom term has passed, speculators are all eager to try, and they were suddenly hit by strange changes in the foreign exchange market. The market has reached a point where it is difficult to stop. The prosperity of the market's entry and exit, and the soaring of market prices, have been rare in recent months. Saigon No. 1 rose from 47 yuan to 49.5 yuan, and small twisted rice was even more prosperous, soaring even more. The opening price was 43.3 yuan, and it rose to 46.3 yuan, a total increase of three yuan compared to the previous day. At noon, many floating investors made profits and released their holdings, suppressing the price by nearly one yuan. However, the spot goods of the relending path were the target of speculators. This rose and that lifted, and the May increase rose to 56.8 yuan, an increase of 4.3 yuan compared to the end of last month. The spot goods had already reached 55.7 yuan, which was also a large increase of over three yuan. The market briefly returned to normal at noon, and then the market rose again in the afternoon, but the main business of those entering and leaving the market was the leather ball business. A total of about 600 tons of returned original packages were transacted, and 8-9,000 packages of spot rice.

Flour Market Turns Firm 107

The flour market turned firm. Although the opening price of the No. 2 flour mill was still 13.5 yuan, the factory was quite likely to raise its prices. Because foreign exchange contracted sharply, the gold market surged, and commodity prices were all driven up. In the morning, old truck brand return goods tightened, and the opening price was over 13.47 yuan. The asking price for the afternoon market was already higher than the factory price. Most of those holding goods were defending the price, intending to wait for a good price, so the total number of transactions for various flours in the entire city was only about 10,000 packages. It was also heard that the customer price for artillery truck was 14.6 yuan, and the low-grade flour No. 4 was 12.4-5 yuan. Customers slightly decorated, but in the afternoon it was heard that the American bank came out to maintain foreign exchange, and the future of commodity prices is unknown.

The wheat market has long been in a flat and soft situation. Because export firms and Japanese factories have been inactive, only Chinese factories are handling affairs. At a time when inventory is drying up, both buyers and sellers are trending toward holding, and sellers are even more determined to sell. It was heard that about 1-2,000 packages of goods delivered to the factory were priced at 21 yuan, but transactions remained deadlocked.

Yarn and Cotton: Yarn Also Soars, Double Horse Jumps 180 Yuan 108

The yarn market soared, and the changes in the situation were truly astonishing. The difference between the opening and closing prices was more than 200 yuan, and the state of the market was as chaotic as hemp. Due to the frequent news of sudden changes in foreign exchange, the price of 20-count Double Horse yarn for May immediately jumped 200 yuan, to 1,730 yuan. With the 70% price added, it has reached around 1,900 yuan. This situation is frightening.

The morning opening for spot yarn was flat because actual sales were weak and market sentiment was flat. In addition, the high and low prices of 20-count yarn were uneven and far apart. The opening price for 20-count variant horse was 1,465 yuan, a drop of 10 yuan. In an instant, news broke that foreign exchange had greatly changed and gold had soared, and the buying atmosphere suddenly became strong, immediately jumping straight to 1,685 yuan. Later, as those taking profits released their holdings, the price fell back to 1,600 yuan, and then rose again to 1,630 yuan at the close. After checking the transaction statistics for half a day, 2,155 packages were transacted. The market price for 20-count variant horse spot jumped 180 yuan. Market Situation Summary 111

Erratic Silk Transactions: Yesterday's silk market was extremely chaotic, mainly due to the sharp contraction of exchange rates, prompting foreign firms to scramble for purchases. Most transactions were based on quotations from the previous day's telegrams, resulting in price discrepancies of three to four hundred yuan compared to the day's market prices. Consequently, silk merchants largely adopted a wait-and-see attitude in the afternoon, ceasing trading activities. Yesterday, Da Chang, Jardine Matheson, and Shin Shing and other firms collectively purchased four hundred bales. White filature and various reel silk grades were traded. All selling prices increased by fifty to two hundred yuan compared to the previous day's records. Although the prevailing sentiment is bullish, the silkworm cocoon harvesting season is approaching, and the rise in silk prices may cause more harm than good to future operations.

Slight Movement in Green Tea Exports: Yesterday, the price of green tea in various European estates was driven by the soaring gold prices and the sharp contraction of foreign exchange rates. Regarding Chunmee and Gunpowder tea, Jardine Matheson, Concordia, Tungkfook, Paochong and other firms purchased a total of over five hundred and ninety boxes of green tea. Selected Chunmee tea was sold at prices ranging from three hundred to three hundred and twenty-eight yuan, unselected Chunmee tea at one hundred and ninety to two hundred and forty yuan, and Gunpowder tea at two hundred and eighty to three hundred and ten yuan.

Soybeans Rise by Four to Five Yuan: Yesterday, the market for miscellaneous grains and soybeans was hit by turbulent waves, causing people to hesitate to sell their goods easily. The market was filled with buying interest but lacked sellers. Speculators were actively entering and exiting the market, creating unusual volatility. Consequently, the soybean market surged by four to five yuan (market price). The bean market rose sharply by one to two yuan.

Golden Needles and Hunan Lotus Seeds Both Rise: Among the northern goods, golden needles, tree ears, and Hunan lotus seeds have seen price increases of ten to twenty yuan due to demand from Hong Kong and their connection to foreign exchange. Tree ears were quoted at three hundred and twenty yuan. Locally grown lotus seeds, previously offered at one hundred and eighty-two yuan, were quoted at two hundred yuan yesterday. Top-grade vegetables, previously at fifty yuan, were quoted at four hundred and sixty yuan, with reported transactions at fifty-five yuan.

Seafood Held Back in Anticipation: Most seafood is imported and thus heavily influenced by foreign exchange rates. Therefore, major seafood dealers are adopting a wait-and-see approach and temporarily withholding sales. The expected price increase is approximately thirty percent.

Woolen Fabrics Continue to Arrive in Shanghai: Imported woolen fabrics from countries such as England, the United States, Japan, and Italy continue to arrive in Shanghai. Most are urgently needed fabrics such as feather yarn wool, heavy tweed, "baratheas", worsted coating, white serge, white drill, and "Wan Li Ding" fabrics. Customs clearance is extremely congested, as most of these goods were sold earlier and are now awaiting delivery upon arrival. Market price: Thursday, May 2, Year 29.

Old News Rehashed: Sixty-Seven Years Ago (372) 112

(Seen in this newspaper, published in the twelfth year of the Tongzhi reign of the Qing Dynasty)

Cricket Tomb 113

A certain person was fond of cricket fighting. In the autumn of the previous year, he obtained a cricket that won repeatedly, earning him over a thousand gold coins. When the cricket died, he placed it in a silver coffin, engraved with a jade tablet, and inscribed it with "General Speedy and Agile". It was buried in the flower bed of the backyard, with a rounded tomb. Last autumn, after the White Dew season, his old addiction resurfaced. He sought crickets everywhere but found none to his liking. One evening, he was walking alone in the backyard when he suddenly heard a cricket chirping sound. Upon listening closely, he realized it was coming from the tomb. He dug up the tomb to find it, but saw nothing. Opening the silver coffin, he found that the cricket he had buried stiff and lifeless was now lively, flapping its wings, baring its fangs, and ready to fight. The man was overjoyed, thinking it was the reincarnation of the general. He took it out and fed it. When he tested it against the crickets he had, they were all easily defeated. He then took it out to gamble a little, and every bet was successful. From then on, he cherished it like a treasure, and would not bet a single fight unless for a large sum. The next day, a guest from Hangzhou visited him, bringing a basin and asking for a bet. The man saw that the guest's cricket was not very strong, so he increased the bet, agreeing to ten gold coins per "flower", with a hundred "flowers" determining the winner. The guest was not satisfied and proposed to add more. So, the two crickets were placed in the basin. As soon as they met, the man's cricket turned around and ran away. When forced to fight again, it jumped around endlessly, and then suddenly died. After the man paid off the bets he lost, he realized that he had used up all the winnings from the previous autumn, and it was still not even half of the debt. This year, after the spring sun greened the backyard, the man idly walked past the cricket tomb and angrily dug up and destroyed the tomb.

Spring and Autumn Annals

The Art of Speaking (2) 114

Even when subjected to great anger, he remained silent. The prophecy of Isaiah perfectly describes Jesus: "He was crucified with criminals, buried with the wicked, although he had committed no crime and no deceit was found in his mouth." The Roman judge, in Caesar's judgment hall, said to Jesus, "Don't you hear how many accusations they are bringing against you?" Jesus did not answer a word, which greatly astonished the judge. When Jesus remained silent, Pilate brought him to the front of the palace and said to the crowd, simply and truthfully, "Behold, the man!" Even when subjected to great anger and injustice, when all his instincts urged him to speak to avoid regret, he remained silent as usual. This requires true courage and true spirit. From this, we can see the greatness of Jesus. Jesus understood the value of silence and strictly controlled his ability to speak. Secondly, we see that Jesus spoke cautiously. When he spoke, he carefully chose his words, selecting those of value and speaking concisely, not wasting a single word. Every word has some meaning for life, and every character reveals his own personality. I remember when the United States held the dedication ceremony at the Gettysburg battlefield, the great American orator Hale spoke for over an hour, while Lincoln only spoke for seven minutes, yet his words have been translated into the languages of the world and passed down for millennia. From the four Gospels, we can see that Jesus's words can be read in thirty-five minutes, so short, yet the most quoted. Thus, the value of words lies not in quantity but in quality. Our fortune, misfortune, joy, and sorrow often come from the words we speak. The ability to speak is our greatest asset, but also our greatest danger. "Who is wise and understanding among you? Let them show it by their good life, by deeds done in the humility that comes from wisdom." For detailed study, please write to P.O. Box 1227.

Re-Emphasizing the "Safety Campaign" 115

– Lessons from the Past

In major cities, the number of innocent people who die under the wheels of vehicles each year is a terrible record. Last autumn, the authorities of the two concessions in Shanghai held a "Safety Campaign", which was a good idea. According to reports at the time, during the period of large-scale publicity and implementation involving filming movies, posting slogans, and students from various schools providing services on the roads, the number of vehicle accidents did decrease. However, although people feel fear towards the threat of death, they quickly forget the warning that "roads are like a tiger's mouth, do not walk in the middle". Drivers also fear legal trouble after causing accidents, but the "I am the only one who matters" mentality continues. Therefore, once the "publicity" period is over, everyone seems to "guarantee safety" and forget everything completely.

The so-called "Safety Campaign" naturally involves cooperation between pedestrians and drivers, but in many cases, there are situations that pedestrians cannot prevent. Let me give you the best example I have at hand, which is the injury to both feet of Yan Chuntang, the owner of Yihua.

The fault was naturally not with Mr. Yan, because no matter how crowded the passengers are, the driver cannot start the car immediately unless the doors are closed. If the ticket seller rings the bell early, then the ticket seller and the driver should jointly bear the responsibility, because they are the closest collaborators on the car.

Furthermore, due to the occurrence of this tragedy, there are a few points that must be said about the drivers and ticket sellers of Route 10 buses – in fact, they are also their faults, because even if they do not cause accidents, their dereliction of duty is a fact.

We know that Route 10 buses are the most crowded vehicles, and it is common for them not to stop due to the large number of passengers at the station (it is hoped that the company can add more vehicles). However, this has caused drivers to develop a habit of sometimes stepping on the accelerator and driving forward even when the car is not very crowded, leaving many passengers waiting at the station. Thus, after one, two, or even three cars have passed, the passengers at the station line up like they are buying cheap rice. In this way, when the fourth car comes, it is naturally impossible to accommodate so many passengers. The ticket seller ringing the bell early occurs at this time, and the tragic incident of the unfortunate passenger having their feet run over also occurs at this time.

This is just one example, and other trams or trolley buses also have this situation.

Let me say it again, the "Safety Campaign" is cooperation between pedestrians and drivers, but deliberately betting one's life and vehicle is ultimately a joke. Therefore, drivers paying attention to their duties is also the way to "safety".

The "Safety Campaign" is not a "fun fair", just as driving is not a simple mechanical task.

"Can't Live On" 116

— Chen Can

Passing by Race Course Road, several rather large, thin chalk characters: "Can't Live On," burst into my sight. Followed by a mother with a drooping head, holding an infant less than a year old in her arms, and beside her, a boy and a girl, silently kneeling and begging for the sympathy of passersby.

"Can't Live On!" What a desperate, simple, and powerful cry, it strongly expresses the desire to survive; it is more direct and to the point than a long and verbose "complaint to the authorities."

A crowd was gathered around, gazing at them, and occasionally one or two passersby would squeeze in to take a look, but then go away looking blank. Are they so heartless? Seeing these people who seem to be straight out of a Masureller woodcut, they are unmoved and do not extend a hand of sympathy. But you are wrong to think so, these hurried and anxious strangers, perhaps they themselves should be classified as "Can't Live On"!

However, on this isolated island, there are also plenty of people living too well: high-rise buildings, beautiful wives and concubines, luxurious clothing and fine food, responding to every beck and call. The urgent, simple, and powerful cry of "Can't Live On," they cannot see it, and will never hear it, because they live in another world.

But please, take out your compassion, you must know that the group of "Can't Live On" are also our descendants of Yan and Huang. According to the meaning of "sharing the same boat in the storm," the valuable things we rescue them from the line of starvation, only require you to moderate your extravagant lifestyles a little, with a small effort, you will help others considerably.

We should enable people who "Can't Live On" to all live on!

A Question 117

— Xin Yin

A little after four o'clock, the tram was so crowded that it was almost impossible to breathe.

At Rue Cardinal Mercier, many passengers got off, and there was much more space on the platform. After the tram started moving, the driver said first:

"Those two 'Chi Laos' have gone. I wonder if the old man had anything stolen?"

"I don't know, I suppose they wouldn't go empty-handed." The ticket seller replied.

A passenger asked, seemingly not understanding:

"What are 'Chi Laos'?"

"Pickpockets!"

"Those two?" The passenger continued to ask.

I did not hear the ticket seller's reply, but wondered in my heart:

"Since you knew, why didn't you catch them?"

Avenue Mesny arrived, and the passengers got off one after another, and I followed and got off the tram too.

After the Rain, a Clear Sky 118

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 23: Old Friends and New Acquaintances, Writing Has Value; Famous Scenic Spots, Well-Managed People

Jin Danyun had already secretly informed Zhu Airen to set her mind at ease. Moreover, the Suliya couple wanted to visit their hospital and infant asylum in a few days. Therefore, Zhu Airen thought: instead of visiting the hospital and infant asylum in a few days, why not visit them now? So she said, "Then after we send Sister Junsu to school today, why not go to our Anle Town to see our country hospital and country infant asylum? If you don't mind the humble accommodations, would you like to have a simple meal with us there?" Jin Danyun said, "No! Our itinerary has already been arranged. After we send Sister Junsu back to school, we will go to Yuantouzhu in Wuxi for lunch. This was arranged in advance, and we are guests of Mr. Xue, an engineer and old classmate of Jiancheng and his wife. This Mr. Xue is the deputy manager and chief engineer of the Taihu Cement Company. In the evening, we will rush to Huzhou and stay at the Huanhu Third Hotel, and someone will also treat us to dinner, namely Jiancheng's elder sister and brother-in-law. They live in Huzhou, which was also arranged in advance. Tomorrow morning, we will return to Jiaxing, and someone has also arranged lunch. After returning to Suzhou from Jiaxing, we might be able to visit Anle Town, and then return to Shanghai." "Zhu Ai" said, "That's fine then! Let's decide on visiting Anle Town tomorrow afternoon. I'll take this ride to return to the hospital. It's just that we're troubling you along the way, which makes us very uneasy. What should we do?" Jin Danyun said, "We're like sisters, why speak so politely?" At that time, the two Miss He originally wanted to invite Lin Jiancheng, Engineer Lin, to see the site of their factory in Freedom Village, which they planned to build. It was just that they were on their honeymoon vacation, so it was difficult to mention it. Today, knowing that they were going to Anle Town tomorrow afternoon, and that Anle Town was not far from Freedom Village, they could take this opportunity to invite the couple to see the factory site in Freedom Village, so that they could have a rough idea of it. At that time, the two Miss He took the opportunity to tell Jin Danyun, and Jin Danyun immediately agreed, saying, "Definitely, and we also want to visit Village Chief Zhu, Mr. Zhu, in Freedom Village. He was still a comrade of my late father, and also the most respected elder by my late father." The two Miss He happened to have this opportunity, and naturally they were overjoyed. As they were talking, the car gradually approached Suzhou, which was a bustling town, and the Bao'en Temple Pagoda in Suzhou was already towering in sight. Mrs. Suliya said, "What is this place?" Wu Junsu said, "This is called Waikuatang, a town in the northeast of Suzhou." So she asked Jin Danyun, "I'll get on the bus here, so I can get to my school."

Entertainment World

A Few Suggestions Regarding Domestic Films 120

— Qiu Xi

In recent years, the production of "historical costume dramas" can truly be described as surging like a storm. Great Wall is invincible, but observing their content, nineteen out of ten take the romantic affairs of "talented scholars and beautiful ladies" as their subject matter. This kind of "historical costume drama" can only suit the tastes of a certain group of people. In the eyes of young children, it does not evoke any interest. Therefore, I hope that the authorities of various domestic film companies, when choosing materials in the future, will carefully consider adopting more good materials related to national child heroes in history, which I believe is also urgently needed by young children!

Living on today's isolated island, the difficulties encountered by young people, and the temptations of evil forces, are all enough to make them numb, sink, and degenerate, because they are far away from the embrace of the motherland. Here, we can use subtle methods to shoot some conscious films to inspire their will, point out their paths, and let them know how they should fight against the strong enemy at hand!

As for the historical data of national child heroes, there are many, such as Zai Qi of the State of Lu in the Spring and Autumn Period, who, in order to defend his motherland and save the country from danger, took up arms and bravely killed the enemy, and the heroic deeds of dying on the battlefield. Shi Tongzi of Jiading in the Ming Dynasty, who made sacrifices to resist the enemy, and Xia Cungu of Songjiang in the late Ming Dynasty—this journal previously published Mr. Haixing's "Child Hero Xia Cungu," saying that Wei Ruohui is now engaged in adapting it into a children's historical drama—when the Qing soldiers went south, he resolutely joined the army to plot the restoration of the country. The stories that can be sung and wept over are all good subjects for realistic shooting.

In addition, there are also the struggle histories of famous people in history during their childhood, which are all worthy of emulation and practice by modern young children.

Review of the Wing On Amusement Society's Charity Performance of "Pan Jinlian" 121

— Wu

The Wing On Amusement Society, organized by colleagues from the Wing On Company, was invited by the Shanghai Relief Committee for Zhongshan Refugees to perform a charity performance at the Lyceum Theatre for eight consecutive evenings. The reporter drove to watch on the evening of the 30th. The performance that evening was the society's newly adapted and improved "Pan Jinlian."

The play lasted four hours. The plot was intense, and the atmosphere was tense all the time. The plot depicts Pan Jinlian as a victim of forced marriage under the feudal system. It was adapted by Mai Youyun, and is sad and beautiful, with profound plots and demanding singing and acting. The playwright's mastery of Chinese classics is profound, and the lyrics are ornate and beautiful, thorough and exquisite. The dialogue in the play is witty and ambiguous, with endless aftertastes. The wording is subtle, and is appreciated by both the refined and the common. Only a master can achieve this.

The protagonist Guo Linshuang's Wu Song is heroic and majestic in appearance, agile and steady in his movements, and has a clear voice. The two scenes of killing his sister-in-law and offering sacrifices to her spirit are passionate, tragic, and touching. His recitations and singing have a magnetic sound, and are mournful and powerful. Zhong Fenghua's Pan Jinlian is also very exquisite in her performance, from the initial gentleness to the subsequent coquetry when teasing her uncle; when rejected, she is both hateful and surprised, and the twists and turns of her emotions are fully conveyed. Her voice is as thin as a gossamer thread, and stops the clouds in their tracks. Mr. Mai plays Ximen Qing, and his free and unrestrained manner gives people a deep impression, and his pronunciation is clear throughout the performance. Liang Yimin portrays Wu Dalang vividly, bringing out his personality perfectly; the scene of saying goodbye to his brother is deeply emotional and sincere. Tang Guanpeng's Uncle Jiu is full of energy, has a mellow singing voice, and is serious in his movements, but is slightly overdone. The other supporting actors are well-matched and complement each other perfectly.

As for all the sets, costumes, props, and lighting, they are luxurious and novel. Reading the society's special publication, I know that "Xi Shi" and "The Peach Blossom Fan" have more nationalistic ideas. I believe that the ticket prices for this charity performance, five yuan, ten yuan, and twenty yuan, are quite expensive, but this is inevitable because it is a charitable event. If the ticket prices could be lowered slightly for general public performances, wouldn't the benefits to the world and people's hearts be great?

British and French Ambassadors Host International Charity Performance 123

— Li Wen

Drama Society Performs Famous Play "Wu Zetian"

When the Shanghai Drama Society was performing at the Lyceum Theatre, there was already news of an international charity performance, but it later subsided. Now, this charity performance has become more concrete. It can be said that the drama circle is having a relationship with the international community for the first time, because it is hosted by the British and French ambassadors and performed by the Shanghai Drama Society. The Drama Society had carefully considered the repertoire for this grand performance. At that time, it was planned to perform a play translated from British and French works. However, thinking that using the Chinese stage techniques, which have not yet reached the pinnacle of perfection, to perform foreign plays, foreign audiences may not be satisfied. So it was decided to perform a play with strong Chinese flavor.

"Wu Zetian" was decided under such circumstances. Wu Zetian is the only female emperor in Chinese history, and many foreigners know about her experiences. This can not only arouse the interest of foreigners, but also allow foreigners to have a real understanding of her. The date of the performance has been decided to be held on the evening of May 22nd, and the ticket prices are divided into two types: five yuan and ten yuan. The Drama Society attaches great importance to this performance, and the selection of actors is especially meticulous (Xia Xia will still play the role of Wu Zetian), and it is scheduled to be previewed once on May 3rd. The ticket prices for this preview will be the same as usual.

Regulations of the American Film Censorship Board - May Our Country's Filmmakers Pay Attention 125

— Dani

On March 31, 1930, the American Film Censorship Board convened all filmmakers to jointly formulate and abide by the following articles. Among them, the "Special Regulations" have excessively detailed outlines, and due to space limitations, it is not convenient to copy them verbatim. Here, the three articles of the main text are excerpted and translated here for the reference of filmmakers in our country. Especially in today's isolated island, the film industry has developed abnormally. Works that inspire justice and promote popular morale are already common, but there are also many that are vulgar and boring. I hope that all filmmakers will correct their mistakes if they have them, and encourage themselves if they do not, which is the motivation for the author to excerpt and translate this article.

Main Text

(1) Productions that are lower than the moral standards of the audience are strictly prohibited. In other words, films that are sufficient to promote the audience's tendency to commit crimes and bad behaviors should be made to disappear.

(2) If it is necessary to change the existing social life system or state due to the needs of the plot, this layer can be accommodated and handled.

(3) Productions that produce ridicule of the law, or indirectly encourage blasphemy of the law are not allowed.

A Record of the Chess Tournament for the Soldiers in Chongqing 126

— Xinsheng

(Chongqing Correspondence) Our country's chess master, Mr. Xie Xiaxun, arrived in Chongqing last month from Kunming. He recently participated in a chess tournament for the soldiers. Here is a brief description:

The preliminary round opened at 7:00 p.m. on April 7th in the hall of the Sino-French-Swiss-Belgian Alumni Association. President Shao Lizi delivered a speech, and Mr. Xie reported on his travels in the south, generally saying: This time he went abroad through the Philippines, Java, Malaysia, and Burma, and all the monthly donations promoted and founded amounted to about 20 million yuan in national currency, and the income from chess tickets was more than 50,000 yuan in national currency, all of which were used to help refugees and plead for the lives of tens of millions of victims in the motherland. Then the chess competition began. At the beginning of the preliminary round, both sides fought fiercely. Then, Mr. Xie personally played blind chess against Chen Xunqu, the top player in the Ministry of Finance. The moves were brilliant, and the audience applauded. As a result, Master Xie won a game, and the preliminary round temporarily came to an end.

The official chess competition opened on the evening of April 11th. The venue was the Social Hall, which was still divided into two major chessboards: Chinese chess and international chess. The Chinese chessboard was arranged side by side on the left and right. Souvenirs from Mr. Xie's trip to the south were hung on the scene, colorful and interesting. First, President Shao Lizi explained the significance of the chess competition, and then Mr. Xie painfully described the similarities and differences between Chinese chess and international chess. Then the general attack began. For a time, the atmosphere was tense, and all the more than a thousand spectators in the audience were concentrating on the two major battlefields in the east and west. The total battle reports for the three nights are listed below:

The 11th night: (1) Ms. Fu Xuewen, the wife of President Shao Lizi, led the ladies' coalition army, and the wife of Commander Gan of the Military Service Department, Ms. Cui Huifang, and Ms. Huang Xiang, faced Ms. Huang Zhuoqun, the wife of Mayor Wu Guozhen, and Chen Weiyu, Sun Bingman, and Chen Daozhu. The notary was the female painter Zhang Hong, the owner of the hall. As a result, each won a game. (2) Xie Shao-shuai Bingyi of the International Chess faced Canadian tiger general Zhou Qiming (transliteration). China won. (3) Fang Qianli, Su Tiande, and others from the coalition army of the Ordnance Department of the Ministry of Military Affairs, faced He Molin, Chen Hu, and others from the coalition army of the Ministry of Communications. The Ordnance Department won the championship in three games. (4) Commander Xie played blind chess against the coalition army of the Ordnance Department, Committee Member Zuo Luhuo, etc. Mr. Xie won.

The 12th night: (1) Lianjunzhu Xiaocen and Yan Chao from the Ministry of Social Affairs and the Ministry of Finance played against the police brigade of the municipal government. The former won. (2) Xie Shao-shuai Bingyi of the International Chess faced Briton Li Tiandan (transliteration). Mr. Xie won two more soldiers and drew the game. (3) The coalition army of the Central Bank faced Ambassador Shao Lizi and Dr. Zheng Manqing of the Anti-Aggression Conference. The Anti-Aggression Conference won the championship in three games. (4) Master Xie played blind chess against the coalition army of Wu Songyao and Hua Peng, etc. of the Military Commission. Mr. Xie drew the game.

The 13th night: (1) Legislator Qi Zhihou played against the coalition army of the Ministry of Economic Affairs. Qi won. (2) Zhu Jianqiu et al. of the Military Commission played against the coalition army of Yin Ziwen et al. of the Tu Shan Yi Society. The Military Commission won the championship in three games. (3) The coalition army of Commander Xie and his son played blind chess against legislators Qi Zhihou and Wang Quan of the Ministry of Military and Political Affairs. Mr. Xie and his son drew the game.

It is heard that the total ticket income for the three nights was more than 7,000 yuan. After the competition, Mrs. Shao awarded the prizes.

Home
